The National Salvation Army Firmly Defends the Fangzheng Area 12

Engaged in Battle with the Japanese Army for Three Days, No Victory Decided

The Japanese Army Occupies Several Towns Along the River North of Harbin

(Harbin) Many battles are currently occurring in various places in North Manchuria. Japanese soldiers departed from the north side of Harbin along the Amur River on steamers, escorted by gunboats. It is reported that they have occupied several towns along the river, but the anti-Manchukuo army is resisting fiercely in Fangzheng. They have been fighting for three days, and the outcome is still undecided. The eastern section of the Chinese Eastern Railway has had its bridges destroyed. Due to the obstruction of the anti-Manchukuo army, they cannot be repaired. Near Mifeng Station, the repair team was bombarded by the army. The Manchukuo army rushed to protect them and engaged the enemy, and they are still fighting. Two more bridges north of Harbin have been destroyed. It is reported that Ma Zhanshan's troops dismantled two bridges on the Hulan and Hailun roads, one 216 meters long and the other 25 meters long. Traffic on the eastern section of the Chinese Eastern Railway is still blocked, and trains only run to Maoershan, which is 70 miles from Harbin. (Reuters telegram, 5th)

(Harbin) On the 3rd, 700 Japanese soldiers and the cavalry regiment of Shen Cheng's army boarded five ships and sailed to Fangzheng for reinforcements. (Special telegram, 3rd)

(Harbin) Gong Changhai's Self-Defense Army bypassed Songban Station on the evening of the 2nd from the left side of Bin County, Heishantou, and approached Feiketou. Xi Qia's army dug trenches for defense. (Special telegram, 3rd)

Six Bridges on the Hasui Line Destroyed 13

(Harbin) Traffic on the Hasui Line was still limited to Maoershan on the 2nd. Telephone communication reached Ujim, but six bridges between Yimianpo and Ujim were destroyed. The Xiaojiu Station railway bridge has not yet been repaired. The Japanese Army's Murai Brigade fought fiercely with the National Salvation Army for an hour near Yimianpo. The National Salvation Army retreated. The Murai Brigade, due to the disruption of traffic, remained near Ujim. The Itoda Brigade of the Japanese Army opening the eastern line arrived in Ujim on the 2nd and will advance to Yimianpo after traffic is restored. (Special telegram, 2nd)

The Japanese Domon Division Opens to Jilin 14

(Harbin) The Japanese Army's Domon Division opened to Jilin on the 1st, and the Hasebe Brigade opened to the Jitun Line. Wang Delin's Big Sword Team besieged Liushugou on the 2nd and dismantled the tracks. The Japanese army in Dunhua went to reinforce. (Special telegram, 3rd)

Li Qingshan's Troops Build Bridges to Cross the River 15

(Harbin) Li Qingshan's troops operated towards Sanchahe and Taolaizhao on the Hachang Line on the 2nd, and built bridges on the Songhua River to cross the army. A team of Xi Qia's army stationed in Sanchahe had an attachment to Li's model. (Special telegram, 3rd)

The Heilongjiang Army Comes Out on the Taoang Line 16

(Harbin) The Taoang Road was closed on the 2nd. Ma Zhanshan's army, Zhu Fengyang's regiment, appeared on the road. Li's regiment stationed in Zhaodong also advanced towards Daxing. The Japanese side's Suzuki Brigade was ordered to go and block it. (Special telegram, 3rd)

7,000 Volunteer Soldiers Besiege Tongliao 17

(Harbin) Tongliao was besieged by 7,000 volunteer soldiers, which was very urgent. The Japanese army, together with Zhang Haipeng's army, went to attack. (Special telegram, 3rd)

500 Soldiers of the Tonghua Garrison Revolted 18

Yanji: It was heard today that 500 soldiers of the Manchukuo army in Tonghua have joined the anti-Manchukuo army and are now advancing towards Andong. (Reuters telegram, 5th)

(Harbin) 3,000 Big Sword Team volunteer soldiers attacked Tonghua. On the 2nd, they fought fiercely with 1,000 Japanese police officers 20 li north of the city. Three Japanese planes went to assist. (Special telegram, 3rd)

The Japanese Armory in Goubangzi Was Bombed 19

Four Japanese Soldiers Killed by Bomb

(Tokyo) According to a telegram from Shenyang, at 10:00 AM today, more than a dozen plainclothes soldiers infiltrated the Goubangzi armory, attempting to destroy the armory. However, when they were installing the explosives, they were discovered by a Japanese patrol, and when they were about to be arrested, the bomb suddenly exploded, and they were able to escape. As a result, four Japanese soldiers were killed and one was injured. (Dentsu News Agency telegram, 5th)

(Shenyang) This morning at 6:00 AM, the volunteer army bombed the Goubangzi armory, killing four Japanese soldiers and injuring one. (Japan United Press telegram, 5th)

The Japanese Man-Mongolia Development Group Encountered Disaster on the Way to Heilongjiang Province 20

Three People Were Killed and Four Were Missing

(Shenyang) A group of ten people from the Man-Mongolia Development Group organized by the Japanese set out from Qiqihar on April 25th. On May 1st, when they were traveling near Gannan, they were attacked by those who looked like bandits. Three were killed, four were missing, and the remaining three escaped and returned to Qiqihar to report everything to the consulate. (Japan United Press telegram, 5th)

(Shenyang) A team of Japanese who departed from Qiqihar on April 25th to engage in survey work returned to Qiqihar yesterday. It is said that they encountered bandits on the way, three were killed, and four were missing. (Reuters telegram, 5th)

Yan Huiqing Will Submit a Memorandum 21

Explanation of the Lytton Report

Japan Neither Obeys the League of Nations Resolution

And Prevents China From Fulfilling Its Obligations

(Geneva) The Chief Chinese Representative, Dr. Yan, will submit a memorandum criticizing the preliminary report of the Lytton Commission of Inquiry to the Secretariat of the League of Nations within one or two days. Dr. Yan spoke to a Reuters interviewer today, briefly stating the contents of his memorandum, saying that the preliminary report of the Commission of Inquiry shows that Japan has not only failed to fulfill the resolution passed by the Executive Yuan on December 10, stipulating that the Japanese army withdraw into the South Manchurian Railway area, but also prevented China from fulfilling its obligations under this resolution. The so-called Chinese obligation is that China is responsible for the safety of life and property of Japanese residents outside the railway area when the Japanese army withdraws. Dr. Yan continued to speak about the activities of the Japanese army, saying that the Japanese have always declared that their military operations in the three northeastern provinces are to suppress bandits, but the Lytton Report shows that Japanese military operations are now being carried out against organized Chinese troops resisting the Manchukuo army. Dr. Yan attaches great importance to this situation and fears that disputes will arise, but said that he will still deal with it with patience, hoping to obtain a final satisfactory solution. (Reuters telegram, 4th)

The Commission of Inquiry Asks the Soviet Union to Provide Information on the Eastern Provinces 27

Litvinov Replied With a Letter of Rejection

(Moscow) Today, local newspapers published the full text of a letter from League of Nations Secretary-General Drummond to Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov, requesting that Soviet officials in Manchuria provide the League of Nations Commission of Inquiry with testimony regarding the local situation, and Litvinov's letter expressing the Soviet government's rejection of this request. In his letter to Litvinov, Drummond relayed the intention of Lord Lytton, saying that if Soviet officials in Manchuria could provide current witness reports regarding the local situation, it would greatly facilitate the work of the Commission of Inquiry, so he specifically sought the Soviet government's opinion on whether it would object to its officials providing such witness reports. In his reply to Drummond, Litvinov said that the Soviet government is willing to do its best to assist any commission of inquiry with the sincerity to reveal the true situation in Manchuria and stop the Chinese affairs. However, the Soviet government is not a member of the League of Nations and did not participate in the League of Nations' discussion of the Chinese incident or the composition of the Lytton Commission of Inquiry. The Commission of Inquiry also does not have a Soviet representative. Therefore, the Soviet government finds it difficult to determine an appropriate attitude towards the reports provided by its officials, and it is even more difficult to bear any responsibility for the conclusions drawn from such reports by the Commission of Inquiry. Under these circumstances, the Soviet government has no choice but to reject the request of the Commission of Inquiry. (Sizhe News Agency telegram, 4th)

Key Points of the County Council Organization Law 38

(Nanjing) The County Council Organization Law stipulates that all counties nationwide must complete the population census within five months, starting from May. After the completion of the autonomous organizations at all levels below the county, the county councils shall be established within three months. For counties with a population of less than 150,000, the number of councilors shall be set at 15. For those with a population of more than 150,000, one councilor shall be added for every 30,000 people. The term of office for councilors is two years, and they can be re-elected. The powers of the county council are to formulate county-specific laws and regulations, review the county's budget and final accounts, manage county finances, raise county public debt, operate county public property and public utilities, and submit matters such as the exercise of initiative and referendum rights by county citizens for deliberation. All citizens of the Republic of China, regardless of gender, who are 20 years of age or older, have resided in the county area for one year or have a residence for more than two years, and are legally registered as voters, have the right to elect county councilors. Those who are 25 years of age or older and have graduated from junior high school or an equivalent school may be elected as county councilors. (5th Special Dispatch)

National product standards are divided into seven grades, with the first grade being those in which capital, management, raw materials, and labor are all Chinese. Foreign News

Hoover Doctrine 62

A New Term Added to International Law

U.S. Undersecretary of State Reaffirms Far East Foreign Policy

Land Acquired in Violation of the Kellogg-Briand Pact Will Not Be Recognized

Reuters, New York, 5th - Acting Secretary of State Castle delivered an important speech here last night, announcing foreign policy, especially regarding the Far East. Castle did not favor any retaliatory actions against any countries and strongly criticized the concept of power on which the League of Nations was built. Castle introduced a new term in international law called the "Hoover Doctrine," which states that land acquired in violation of the Kellogg-Briand Pact will not be recognized.

National News Agency, Washington, 4th - Today, U.S. Undersecretary of State Castle stated in a speech at the American International Justice Society that when the United States declared that it could not recognize situations created by methods that violate the Kellogg-Briand Pact, it had inserted the edge of the Kellogg-Briand Pact into the Manchurian crisis. This "Hoover Doctrine" is a contribution by the United States to limiting the ability of countries to use force as an instrument. The United States rejected the proposal of economic retaliation because it would only unfairly treat others and harm civilized nations, ultimately leading to war. On the contrary, the "Hoover Doctrine" allows the United States to remain unentangled while at the same time demonstrating its willingness to cooperate with other countries. He pointed out that the League of Nations' recent endorsement of this doctrine is proof of its value and effectiveness.

U.S. Senator Explains Shipbuilding Plan 63

Indirectly Warns Japan

The Authority of Treaties is Almost Completely Destroyed

Only by Strengthening Naval Defenses

Reuters, Washington, 4th - During a meeting of the Senate Naval Affairs Committee today, Senator Hale began a campaign to pass a bill to build ships to the treaty limit, saying that the United States should have a navy capable of avoiding war. The passage of this bill would strengthen the hand of the U.S. representative in Geneva. Hale went on to describe the tragic situation in the Far East, saying that the treaty in which we have absolute faith has now completely failed in its current effect. Its authority has been lost, and we can no longer rely on it for future security. The U.S. Navy today is much weaker than before the Washington Conference. Hale warned Japan that the U.S.'s failure to strengthen its Pacific naval defenses is based on treaties guaranteeing China's territorial integrity and the open door policy.

Unexpected Discussion on the Far East Situation 64

Japan Endangers Peace with Undeclared War

Italy's Interests in China Suffer Great Losses

Once China's Politics and Economy Recover

It Will Have Great Power in the World

Reuters, Rome, 4th - Italian Prime Minister Grandi said in the House of Representatives today that while disarmament was being discussed in Geneva, the sound of cannons in the Far East was deafening. The world now has no so-called remoteness. Countries like Italy, which have global relations, no longer have a distinction between near and far. From the perspective of establishing a field and from the special standpoint of Italian interests, both China and Japan are related to Italy. The undeclared war in the Far East has lasted for eight months. The Italian government, together with the powers concerned in the Pacific, has adopted an impartial attitude in order to prevent the expansion of the conflict and to obtain a rapid and fair resolution that conforms to the principles of the Paris Pact, the League of Nations Charter, and the Nine-Power Treaty. Grandi then detailed Italy's special relationship with China, saying that Italy has 500 missionaries in China, divided into 29 missionary regions, as well as the Tianjin Concession, Italian banks, consular jurisdiction, Boxer indemnity, and former Austrian debts. In Shanghai, there is also the Italian Chamber of Commerce, and Italian shipping on the Yangtze River has a tendency to develop commercially. Italy and Shanghai also have maritime shipping connections. Grandi went on to say that in this conflict, the interests equal to Italy's special interests are the political interests concentrated on the balance of power in the Pacific and the status stipulated in the treaty. This conflict is now happening in a country with a huge population. Although this country is now in turmoil, with its 400 million people, once its politics and economy recover, it will inevitably have great power in world relations. However, at a time when international unity is urgently needed to overcome the economic crisis, this conflict endangers world peace. The diplomatic negotiations in Shanghai seem to be approaching the end stage at this time, but the situation is still in danger of renewed disputes, because the unified cooperation that is indispensable for adjusting various international relations in the Far East does not yet seem to be fully mature. Nevertheless, this reason must not make us abandon the hope that the Far East conflict can be resolved amicably and satisfactorily through the good cooperation of the relevant powers in maintaining peace in the Far East. Grandi also spoke of the disarmament conference, saying that there was too much discussion and too many proposals in Geneva, but the results were minimal. He doubted whether the hearts of the people of the world could wait long without demanding a clarification of the fundamental positions of the countries.

Major Disarmament Debate 65

Britain and the United States Advocate Abolishing Submarines

Japanese Representatives Strenuously Argue Against Abolition

France Takes a Stubborn Stance

The Conference Makes No Progress

National News Agency, Geneva, 4th - In today's Naval Committee of the Disarmament Conference, the American and Japanese representatives once again held different views. American representative Stebbins argued that aircraft carriers are defensive weapons rather than offensive weapons. Japanese representative Sato said that aircraft carriers and all warships equipped with aircraft landing decks are the most advantageous weapons of aggression in modern warfare. After abolishing them, the naval strength stipulated in the Washington and London conventions will not be significantly affected. He also said that aircraft carriers are not needed unless a fleet is taking aggressive action. He greatly agreed with Stebbins' claim that aircraft carriers are the most effective weapons against submarines, but believed that this alone proves that they are offensive weapons because submarines are defensive weapons. He also said that Japan does not oppose allowing warships to carry several aircraft for reconnaissance purposes, but if a fleet has aircraft carriers and bombers, it will be easier to commit acts of aggression in distant seas and increase the fleet's offensive power. British representative Monsell said that the offensive capabilities of aircraft carriers are somewhat exaggerated. This type of warship has thin armor and is a larger target for enemy attacks, so it is the most vulnerable among all types of warships. However, he also agreed to limit the number and size of aircraft carried by aircraft carriers. He also said that a fleet near enemy territory is not necessarily an act of aggression, especially when the country has remote overseas territories. Later, French representative Dumont gave a lengthy and thoughtful speech, saying that submarines are only sufficient to threaten battleships. France must have submarines as a supplement because it has too few battleships. German representative Rheinbaben argued that the interpretation of submarines as offensive weapons in the Treaty of Versailles should be accepted. It is now expected that submarines will become the target of the next heated debate.

Reuters, Geneva, 5th - After struggling to discuss the British proposal to abolish submarines as offensive weapons, the Naval Committee of the Disarmament Conference today failed to reach any resolution. Therefore, the issue of naval mines was discussed. The British representative said that Britain advocates that if submarines are abolished, then "contact mines" in the sea should also be abolished. The Italian representative said that if submarines are abolished, then battleships should also be abolished. The Polish representative said that submarines are only defensive weapons to resist superior navies. However, Poland is prepared to follow the major countries that signed the London Naval Treaty in this matter. American representative Stebbins strongly argued against submarines and said that if submarines are not completely abolished, the United States intends to establish a strong submarine base in the Philippines.

National News Agency, Geneva, 5th - At 10 a.m. this morning, the Naval Committee of the Disarmament Conference convened. The Japanese representative attacked the British and American propositions, arguing that submarines are defensive weapons rather than offensive weapons and should not be included in the list of abolitions. Once they are abolished, countries with strong navies can roam the seas without interference, and countries with weak navies will have no way to guarantee their national defense security. This will lead to stronger countries becoming stronger and weaker countries becoming weaker. Japan also opposed the British proposal to limit the tonnage of submarines because countries with longer coastlines need larger submarines. Therefore, Japan argues that submarines not exceeding 2,000 tons should be classified as defensive weapons, and the strength of submarines should not be strictly limited unless it is considered in relation to the strength of other warships.

National News Agency, Geneva, 5th - This morning, the Geneva Daily commented on the discussions of the technical committee in recent days, believing that the Disarmament Conference may soon drift into a completely deadlocked situation. The newspaper, which often reflects France's attitude towards international issues, claimed that the Disarmament Conference is making backward progress, and this deeply regrettable development is not unrelated to France's stubborn attitude. It also said that after adopting a resolution with completely unambiguous terms, advocating the abolition of offensive weapons, the Disarmament Conference entrusted the experts with the arduous task of defining offensive weapons. However, the experts in Paris in 1919 only needed 48 hours to define the types of offensive weapons that Germany was not allowed to possess. The experts in Geneva in 1931 seem to be inheriting the legacy of their predecessors, reaching a conclusion that there are no offensive weapons in the world.

Stimson Departs Europe to Return to the United States 66

Havas, Cannes, France, 4th - U.S. Secretary of State Stimson, although he suffered a cold while in Geneva, spending most of his stay in bed, still held important talks with key political figures from major European countries on several occasions. He recently embarked on the Fulgoriana ship to return to New York, accompanied by several specialist members of the U.S. delegation to the Disarmament Conference.

Mount Asama Erupts 67

Japanese Union, Tokyo, 5th - Mount Asama, a famous volcano in Japan, erupted at 6:30 a.m. this morning, with a loud noise and black smoke rising into the sky, obscuring the sunlight and looking very tragic.

"Honor Killing" Case Sentenced 68

Four Defendants Each Sentenced to Ten Years in Prison

But Released After One Hour of Imprisonment

National News Agency, Honolulu, 4th - The so-called "honor killing" case in Honolulu suddenly ended today. First Lieutenant McHugh of the U.S. Navy, his mother-in-law, and two sailors were initially declared guilty of manslaughter by a jury last Friday. Today, the judge sentenced each to ten years in prison. Then, Honolulu Governor Judd issued an order to commute the sentence, reducing the ten-year imprisonment to one hour, to be served at the Iolani Palace, the location of the Honolulu legislature. Upon completion of the one-hour period, they were immediately released. The case was originally scheduled to be sentenced on Friday, so no one knew of today's sudden ending. When the news of the verdict spread, the palace was crowded with spectators. The palace was the former palace of the Hawaiian king before the United States annexed the island. The case had attracted great attention from Americans due to racial views and other reasons. Although the jury reduced the murder charge to manslaughter, Americans were still extremely indignant. There were threats to boycott the jury and proposals to ask Congress to pardon the four defendants. American customs have always had a kind of unwritten law, still passed down from colonial times, that people of color who rape white women can be executed by private justice. Therefore, although the murdered Hawaiian, Kahahawai, was only a suspect with insufficient evidence, and was shot and killed by Lieutenant McHugh, the Americans, bound by custom, naturally had different views. Therefore, there was this special sympathy for McHugh's conviction. The authorities in Hawaii, to prevent the occurrence of extrajudicial action, advanced the sentence today. In the morning, the defense lawyer, prosecutor, and judge consulted, and then the four defendants were brought to court, the verdict was announced, and the governor's commutation order was immediately announced.

League of Nations Investigation Team's Words and Actions in Shenyang 69

Fin

Raising Questions During Meetings with Japanese Officials

Avoiding Surveillance, Meetings Held at Own National Consulates

Glimpses of Representative Koo's Talks with Japanese Reporters

Shenyang Special Correspondent: After arriving in Shenyang and resting for a day, the League of Nations Investigation Team officially visited Japanese Acting Consul-General in Shenyang, Mr. Morishima Mamoru, on the 23rd. They inquired about the events surrounding the September 18th Incident, Sino-Japanese relations, and the issue of parallel railway lines. Morishima spoke volubly, denouncing the former Northeast officials as muddleheaded and lawless. On the 24th, the team officially visited Commander of the Kwantung Army, Honjo Shigeru, who hosted a banquet. Subsequently, both sides held talks for two to three hours daily, also for the purpose of studying the September 18th Incident. Sir Lytton, Brigadier-General Claudel, and Major-General McCoy raised various questions, such as: why such a large-scale war was necessary for such a minor railway issue; also, what was heard in Peiping from the former Northeast leader Zhang Xueliang was obviously different from what the Japanese side stated. The Japanese side strongly defended themselves and presented so-called "evidence."

The investigation team's stay here seems to have three reasons: (1) The League of Nations Council will hold a meeting on May 1st, and a first report must be completed before then; (2) The battles regarding Changchun, Jilin, Qiqihar, and Jinzhou still need to be discussed with the Commander of the Kwantung Army; (3) Transportation north of Harbin is very difficult, and for safety reasons, the itinerary is still under study.

For convenience and freedom, each commissioner meets, convenes meetings, and writes reports at their own national consulate. At the British consulate, so-called "farmer representatives," "Korean people representatives," and representatives from Japanese and Manchukuo newspapers visit daily. The team sends personnel to receive them and accept their statements.

Personnel from the Chinese delegation reside in the Yamato and Oriental Hotels, and detectives accompany them in and out, ostensibly for protection. Representative Koo is in contact with the investigation team daily and communicates with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. His work is very busy, and he only takes walks in Chiyoda Park and Kasuga Town in the evening. On the night of the 23rd, consuls from various countries stationed in Shenyang held a grand social gathering at the Yamato Hotel to welcome the investigation team. Although Representative Koo was on the guest list, he has never danced during this time of national crisis. Other members of the delegation gather in room 221 of the Yamato Hotel every day to discuss and report on their observations.

The investigation team's report may be sent to Geneva today or tomorrow. The date of departure north is scheduled for Monday (May 2nd). The itinerary plans to stay in Changchun for one day, return to Jilin on the same day, stay in Harbin for seven days, and Qiqihar for two days. The rest will be decided on an ad hoc basis. Representative Koo insists that Heihe (Blagoveshchensk) must be visited. Except for Harbin, there are no large hotels, and transportation is inconvenient. It is also necessary to travel by plane. Therefore, the number of accompanying personnel must be greatly reduced. On the Chinese side, there will be about six or seven people at most. Mr. Zhang Weibin, who is familiar with the situation in Jilin Province, will return after accompanying them to Changchun. Mr. Yang Chengji, who is familiar with the situation in Heilongjiang Province, will return after accompanying them to Harbin. Further reductions may follow. Except for one or two people left in Shenyang to take care of luggage, all other personnel will return to Peiping via Dalian at the same time. Among the journalists accompanying the team, there were originally three. Now, by drawing lots, only Mr. Bao Jingan will go as the representative.

The investigation team will return to Shenyang in three weeks, stay for three days, go to Dalian, stay for another three days, and return to Peiping. They will spend two months organizing the materials gathered and considering them, and then travel east to contact the Japanese government and then return to China to contact the Chinese government before beginning to write the report.

Representative Koo has come here with a spirit of great fearlessness. Therefore, every word and deed has become material for newspapers. At 4:30 p.m. on April 22nd, he officially met with Japanese journalists at the Yamato Hotel in Shenyang at their request. The questions and answers were quite interesting and are recorded here for amusement.

(Question) Has the itinerary been decided? (Answer) As far as I know, it has not yet been decided. (Question) Will you act in concert with the other commissioners? (Answer) The task of the participating members is to assist the investigation team to fully accomplish its mission. I and the Japanese participating member have the same status and will naturally take concerted action with the other commissioners. (Question) What is your opinion regarding Manchukuo's rejection of you? (Answer) This investigation is based on the League of Nations resolution of December 10th last year. This resolution was recognized by both China and Japan. As a participating member of the investigation team, I cannot but participate in the investigation. (Question) Hasn't Manchukuo declared that it will arrest you? (Answer) Whether an investigation is possible is a matter for the investigation team. I do not need to answer. However, the investigation team has come for peace in East Asia and aims to ascertain the truth of the matter. Manchukuo's rejection of me is truly incomprehensible. (Question) What is your opinion regarding Russia's request to replace its consul in Heihe? (Answer) I only learned about this from the newspaper today. I cannot answer whether the government has received notification. (Question) What is the National Government's observation of Manchukuo? (Answer) I have been away from Nanjing for a long time because I am participating in the investigation team and cannot answer. (Question) But what is your personal opinion? (Answer) This matter is very important and I cannot answer casually. (Question) The National Government has posted slogans such as Japan's annexation of Manchuria. What is your opinion on this? (Answer) I don't remember. (Question) What is your personal opinion regarding Sino-Japanese relations? (Answer) Sino-Japanese relations in recent months have not been a pleasant phenomenon. China and Japan are natural neighbors, interdependent like lips and teeth. I have long heard of the idea of co-existence and co-prosperity. However, the current situation has reached such a state that unless there is eternal hostility, there will be no day for reconciliation. If we are willing to co-exist and co-prosper, we must find another path. The disputes that have arisen today are not entirely due to China. I dare to say that the deterioration of Sino-Japanese relations cannot be said to be Japan's fault and China's right, nor can it be said to be China's fault and Japan's right. The process of mutual accusations cannot be determined now. However, misunderstandings between the two countries must be one of the reasons. To resolve these misunderstandings, we need far-sightedness and effort. However, judging from the current situation, not only is it impossible to resolve misunderstandings, but there is a trend to make them increasingly serious. Therefore, I cannot help but feel very sorry for the occurrence of this fact. (Question) Chinese education pays attention to anti-foreignism, especially anti-Japanese. What is your opinion? (Answer) Matters that easily cause misunderstandings are also easy to find solutions to. (April 29th)

Director of the American Far Eastern Bureau Discusses the Spirit of the Nine-Power Treaty 70

If One Country Infringes Upon the Common Interests of All Countries

The United States Should Adopt a Coordinated Policy with All Countries

The Osaka Asahi Shimbun reported that Stanley Hornbeck, Director of the American Far Eastern Bureau, expressed his views on the Far East issue at a meeting of the International Law Association on the 29th of last month, clarifying the position of the United States. He said that the United States has always respected the principles of other countries' legitimate and vested rights, and, based on the most-favored-nation clause, promotes equality of commercial opportunity, avoids alliances and aggression, and opposes any country obtaining improper rights through coercion. The United States has adopted these points as its foreign policy. Although the United States has not formally joined the League of Nations, it has always cooperated with the League to maintain this purpose. Originally, the US policy towards China was based on the Nine-Power Treaty. The US government's emphasis on the Nine-Power Treaty originally hoped that the signatory countries would respect the spirit of the treaty and be bound by the treaty. All countries that signed the treaty should enjoy its actual rights and interests. Therefore, the United States bases its historical policy towards China on the spirit of the Nine-Power Treaty. At the same time, all countries with rights and interests in the Far East have been consistent in principle since the beginning of the 20th century, that is, the signatory countries should guarantee the overall and ultimate interests of all in the treaty, so that a balance of power can be established in the Far East. If two of the signatory countries have a dispute, the United States should adopt reasonable and fair means to try its best to maintain this treaty, and resolve the dispute under coordination with the countries concerned. The United States and Japan are the two major powers in the Pacific, and the relationship is very important. Recalling that the participating countries in the Washington Conference were all countries with vested interests in China, therefore, the political and economic development in the Far East must respect the fundamental rights and interests of the countries concerned. No country can enjoy rights alone, nor can it bear obligations alone. In this way, world peace can be maintained. If one country infringes upon the common interests of all countries, a peaceful situation cannot be maintained. All countries must never allow the common interests of the world to be trampled upon by one country. In short, in order to maintain peace and uphold the treaty, the United States government should adopt a coordinated policy with all countries. Former Secretary of State Stimson's official statement to Senator Borah in a letter was based on this principle, so as to avoid conflicts between China and Japan, and so on.

Hebei Province Implements Official Opium Sales 71

Monthly Income Approximately One Million Yuan

And Will Encourage Farmers to Grow Opium

Tianjin Correspondent: Official opium sales in the North have been openly implemented. According to investigations, the organizers are the Revenue Raising Committee. The members of this committee are all valiant and martial current military leaders. The reason is that the 200,000-plus troops stationed in Hebei and Chahar provinces have been in arrears for several months. The troops in Shanxi and Suiyuan provinces were originally subsidized by Zhang Xueliang. Since the September 18th Incident, subsidies have been stopped. The difficult situation in Shanxi and Suiyuan is equal to that of Hebei and Chahar. Although the provincial and municipal governments have reduced staff and salaries, subsidies to the military are actually limited. The Financial Reorganization Committee is also at a loss. The Revenue Raising Committee has no alchemic touch to turn base metal into gold. They will naturally choose any means as long as they can raise funds. Official opium sales are the only way to generate revenue. Zhang Xueliang gave his permission and cautioned them to handle it secretly. The general headquarters for official sales in Hebei Province is the Northern Company, organized by powerful figures. It was initially located in Tianjin Special District Three. Because the opium soil passed through the Italian Concession, 60,000 taels were seized. After repeated negotiations, it has not been returned. After this blow, the company moved to Special District Two. Large quantities of opium soil arrived in Tianjin and were unloaded at the new railway station. Originally, they intended to sell openly, but fearing public disapproval, they are currently selling semi-openly, issuing destruction permits, and temporarily not implementing license fees and lamp taxes for establishing opium addiction treatment centers. People who traffic in opium must go to the company to purchase destruction permits to pass unhindered. Policemen and soldiers not only do not stop them, but also provide protection. The destruction permit is shaped like a commemorative stamp, costing two yuan each. Each bag of opium soil (weighing 20 taels) is affixed with one stamp, which allows passage within the region. If transporting from this region to another, the cost doubles. For example, from Rehe to Tianjin, each bag must be affixed with four yuan worth of destruction permits (the same from Tianjin to Peiping or from Peiping to Tianjin). If transporting from Suiyuan through Zhangjiakou and Peiping to Tianjin, each bag must be affixed with eight yuan worth of destruction permits. If the number of destruction permits affixed is insufficient during inspection by police and soldiers along the way, the penalty is doubled. In recent days, many people who trafficked in opium have been detained and fined because they were not familiar with the regulations. After the implementation of this official sale, Rehe opium soil has sold well in the Peiping and Tianjin areas. Suiyuan opium soil is selling slowly due to heavy taxes. According to insiders, Hebei Province's monthly opium revenue is about one million yuan, while monthly expenses are 600,000 yuan. In reality, only 400,000 yuan can subsidize the military. The Revenue Raising Committee, in order to plan for the long term, fears that after official sales, the number of addicts will increase, and the source will be limited, so supply will not meet demand in the long run. Therefore, they plan to order each county magistrate to encourage farmers to grow opium, which will not only avoid a lack of sources, but also allow them to collect opium seedling taxes, increasing revenue. Such poisoning of the people is hateful. Fortunately, it is now the end of spring, and it is no longer the time to grow opium, so it will have to be implemented in the autumn. (May 2nd)

He Yingqin Issues Speech on Bandit Suppression in Three Provinces 72

Drawing Up a New Detailed Plan for Bandit Suppression

Total of More Than 200,000 Troops in Jiangxi, Guangdong, and Fujian

Nanchang Correspondent: Minister of Military Affairs and concurrently Commander-in-Chief of Bandit Suppression in the Three Provinces, He Yingqin, recently issued a statement on the suppression of the Red bandits, stating, "I was ordered last year to come to Jiangxi to suppress the bandits and have been stationed in Jiangxi for nearly a year. I had intended to clear out the Red bandits in Jiangxi Province as soon as possible under a certain plan to relieve the people from their suffering. However, due to the impact of the situation and diplomacy, the bandit suppression plan and the bandit suppression troops could not be used freely. Although the main force of the Red bandits has suffered great injuries, the remnants have fled into the mountains, gathering and dispersing unpredictably, and have not been completely eliminated as a whole. Like a prairie fire, it is still a major problem on the borders of the three provinces of Jiangxi, Guangdong, and Fujian. Speaking of this, it is extremely painful. Those in southern Jiangxi, such as the remnants of Peng Dehuai and Li Mingrui, previously gathered crowds to besiege Ganzhou, and their momentum was very fierce. Relying on the efforts of the officers and soldiers of my 18th Army and Ma Brigade to advance in suppression, they were finally completely defeated. The strength of the Red bandits has been greatly damaged. Those who are still rampant are the Mao Zedong and Lin Biao factions occupying Zhangzhou. The Red bandits have been entrenched in Jiangxi for several years, burning, killing, looting, and turning the land into a scorched earth. Recently, they have realized that they cannot receive supplies of weapons, ammunition, and food, so they have to seek other paths, and thus have the intention of fleeing into Fujian Province. However, since Guangdong Province has increased troops and divided them into Fujian and Jiangxi, joining the original military strength of Jiangxi and Fujian provinces, the total number is more than 200,000. As long as they are under a unified command under the overall plan, and given a reasonable period of time, it is not difficult to completely eliminate the Red bandits. I have come to Jiangxi Province again to understand the latest situation of the Red bandits and to inspect the deployment of our troops for suppression, so as to draw up a new detailed plan for advancing in suppression. Then, according to the plan, we will do it step by step in a practical way, with the overall goal of eliminating the Red bandits. However, we must know that the organized bandits must be completely defeated by the strength of the army. How can we completely eliminate the scattered bandits lurking in various places? With regard to clearing the household registration, handling the baojia system, receiving refugees, prospering the countryside, and propagating the Three People's Principles, the power of party affairs and politics must be used. If the power of the party and the government cannot cooperate, then when the army arrives, the bandits will divide into smaller units, avoid the real and attack the virtual, and scatter and gather indefinitely. If this continues, the power of the Red bandits will only increase day by day. Also, transportation is extremely important for bandit suppression. When I was in Nanjing, I had already made suggestions to the central government and discussed with the chairman to complete the construction of Jiangxi Province's highways as soon as possible, and to lay light railways in 100 important areas. With convenient transportation, the troops can be mobilized quickly, and the supply of supplies will be easy. The Red bandits will naturally have nowhere to escape, and it will be easy to gather and annihilate them. The personnel who came with me this time are extremely simple. Because I have important responsibilities in the Ministry of Military Affairs, I will not be stationed permanently in Nanchang in the future. I must return to Nanjing every two months to handle important ministry affairs. As for the new appointments announced by the central government of me and Chen Bonan as commander-in-chief and deputy commander-in-chief of bandit suppression, this is only for the convenience of command and is a temporary operational command nature, which is different from a fixed position. I have not yet considered whether to formally take office, because the Minister of Military Affairs has the power to order the national army." (May 2nd)

Zhang Xianglin Passes Through Jinan 73

Investigation Team Will Prepare Report in Qingdao

Jinan Correspondent: Zhang Xianglin, Director of General Affairs and concurrently Director of Propaganda of the Chinese Delegation to the League of Nations Investigation Team, previously went to Peiping with the investigation team from Shanghai. Due to a sudden attack of lower back pain, he could no longer go to the Northeast and temporarily stayed in Peiping. The delegation appointed Zhang as the Director of the Shanghai Office. Zhang passed through Jinan from Peiping early this morning (1st). According to Zhang's conversation at the station, after the investigation team arrived in Dalian, they were monitored everywhere and their actions were no longer free. This was especially true for our delegation. Except for places permitted by the Japanese, there was danger if they went beyond the permitted boundaries. Although our delegation could communicate with Peiping by telegram, under strict surveillance, they could not speak freely. In the international community, diplomats have always been relatively free. Today, in the Northeast, a bad precedent has been set in diplomatic history. Representative Koo has come here with great determination, ignoring any intimidation, and various circles in Nanjing and Shanghai have repeatedly sent telegrams supporting him and urging him to work hard to complete his mission, so he went there resolutely. However, after arriving in the Northeast, his actions were completely restricted, making the investigation work extremely difficult. For example, the Beidaying, the site where the Northeast Incident originated, is an extremely important place, but the investigation team was prevented from going there to inspect it. Representative Koo decided to go to Changchun, but his actions were still monitored. Since his actions were not free, even if he went, he was afraid that it would be difficult to achieve any results. As for the location where the investigation team will prepare the report, it was originally planned to be in Beidaihe, but the Japanese strongly opposed it, which has become a thing of the past. It will probably be in Qingdao. Therefore, the investigation team is scheduled to go to Qingdao for summer retreat after the Northeast affairs are completed to prepare the report. The Director of our country's delegation's office in Peiping is Wang Guangqi, and I am the Director of the Shanghai office. This time I came to Shanghai to handle unfinished matters in Shanghai. Our delegation feared that they would not be free after arriving in the Northeast and that important documents might be lost, so they were not brought along. (1st)

Local News

Cai Tingkai's Address to Officers and Soldiers 75

On the 28th of last month, Commander Cai Tingkai addressed the officers and soldiers of the 60th Division at Fengqiao, Suzhou, saying: "Officers and soldiers, today your division commander asked me to speak with you. Many of you are new recruits, but the discipline and appearance on the training ground are neat and solemn, which the commander finds very satisfactory. You new recruits are now armed comrades of the 19th Route Army. Before joining, why did you want to join this group? And after joining, how should you become an outstanding member of the 19th Route Army? You must deeply understand this. Perhaps some of you eagerly joined our army due to a temporary patriotic impulse, initially not understanding the meaning of being a soldier. What is the meaning of being a soldier? First, you must have a clear purpose, dedicating yourself to the country and disregarding personal interests. Second, you must be prepared, with military knowledge and skills. With military preparation, you can use all your knowledge and skills to achieve the purpose of being a soldier, protecting the country and its people. Only then does being a soldier have meaning, only then can you be a loyal comrade of the 19th Route Army, and only then are you worthy of being called a revolutionary soldier.

Excluding Guangdong, Guangxi, the Northeast, Yunnan, Guizhou, and Sichuan, our country currently has 90 divisions of the army. Such an astonishing number of standing soldiers is unprecedented in any modern country. Judging by the quantity of our army, China's national defense should be very solid. However, the reality is not so. The three northeastern provinces have been taken by Japan without much effort. Then Japan invaded Shanghai. After the January 28th Incident occurred, only our 19th Route Army and the 5th Army resisted them. Originally, China had over a hundred divisions (including those in Guangdong, Guangxi, etc.) of standing troops. Why were only two units fighting the Japanese army? The reasons are long and complex. In summary, after the corrupt roots were planted during the late Qing dynasty, there was no provision for national defense, the army lacked strict organization and training, transportation was inconvenient, and the communist bandits were rampant. As a result, Japan increased its land forces by more than 100,000. When the frontline fighting was most intense, the 19th Route Army and the 5th Army were still struggling to support it. Other troops in other areas were unable to provide support due to various constraints. Eventually, we had no choice but to retreat to the second line of defense. If China were not so corrupt internally and could use even half of its existing hundred-plus divisions to contend with the brutal Japanese, although we could not say we would directly attack Tokyo, we could at least preserve our territory and not lose an inch of land to the brutal Japanese. We always think that our daily food, clothing, housing, and all supplies come from the people's hard-earned money. If we cannot absolutely protect public order internally and cannot resist foreign invasion and defend the country externally, then as commander, I am very ashamed. You must have the same feeling. But is it enough for us to just feel ashamed? With our remaining lives, how should we strive to repel the brutal invaders, recover lost territories, and remove the shame in our hearts? You new comrades, since you are willing to be wholeheartedly loyal and be good revolutionary soldiers, how should we strengthen our strength to prepare for sacrifices against foreign enemies? In the recent battles in Shanghai by the 19th Route Army and our beloved 5th Army, although the sacrifices were great, the belief of all officers and soldiers in sacrificing themselves for the country has become even stronger and not diminished in the slightest. This is very comforting to me as commander. Speaking of the military pay of our army, I might as well briefly report on the financial situation of our army here. Since June of last year, when the 19th Route Army was responsible for the third phase of bandit suppression in Jiangxi, all military pay has been directly distributed by the central government (before June of last year, it was allocated nearby from Guangdong's national tax revenue). The original plan was to disburse a total of one million yuan per month for all marching and combat expenses and pay, but in reality, less than 80% was received. After November, it was reduced to 500,000 yuan. Eventually, due to the central government's financial difficulties, only an actual average of more than 300,000 yuan per month was received until March of this year. Just imagine how much pay your division demands each month. How can this meager sum of more than 300,000 yuan be distributed? Have you thought about the difficulties involved? Since the January 28th Shanghai Incident occurred, temporary military spending has suddenly increased. However, we have been able to make arrangements in every aspect and also provide assistance to friendly forces. Besides the more than 300,000 yuan allocated by the central government each month, where did this money come from? You probably all know that it all comes from the hard-earned money and enthusiastic support of compatriots from all walks of life in Shanghai, Guangdong, and various ports. How great our sacrifices are to resist the brutal Japanese invasion is our duty. We are not selling our fame with our blood and flesh, nor are we tools for anyone. We are sacrificing for the survival of the Chinese race based on our conscience and inner motivation. We truly feel ashamed and grateful for the excessive help from the people. In this battle, even after being ordered to retreat, some of you even failed to strictly abide by discipline and disturbed our compatriots. Although the matter is trivial, I feel more heartbroken and sad about this behavior than anything else. Also, some wounded soldiers caused trouble in the hospital, thinking that because they were injured, they could act arrogantly. These ignorant actions are truly hateful. Soldiers are supported by the state, and it is their duty to die on the battlefield. Can they act arrogantly just because they are injured? It has been reported that a small number of wounded soldiers ran to the concessions in Shanghai to cause trouble, were beaten and kicked by foreign police officers until they were half-dead, and then thrown out of the concessions. As dignified Chinese soldiers, they did not die on the battlefield but were trampled on by foreigners to this extent. This fully demonstrates that Chinese soldiers are uneducated and do not know how to respect themselves. You are all men of integrity, can you tolerate such humiliation? From now on, all wounded soldiers must absolutely abide by discipline. Otherwise, I will severely punish them. This is a bad impression that you have given me in terms of discipline, and I want you to pay close attention and correct it. Next, let me talk about the immaturity of the national character of our country. The prevalence and deep-rootedness of individualism and family concepts are the main causes of the nation's weakness today. Because education is not widespread, the vast majority of the people do not have the opportunity to receive education, resulting in the illiteracy rate reaching over 80% of the total population. The national character is immature due to lack of education, and coupled with the particularly strong traditional family concept that has been around for thousands of years, most people only recognize their families and hardly know what the country is. If the national situation is like this, how can the country become prosperous and strong? During the fierce battles between our army and the brutal Japanese in Shanghai, the communist bandits in Jiangxi not only failed to be awakened by the national crisis and unite to resist foreign aggression but instead took the opportunity to launch a fierce attack on Ganzhou, attempting to seize the important southern Jiangxi city to disrupt our rear. This kind of behavior is tantamount to supporting the brutal Japanese and acting as their internal accomplice. We know that there are also communist parties in Japan and other countries. However, they are unwilling to disrupt their country from within and divide their government's strength against foreign aggression when their country is in trouble. Comparing the two, we can know what the Chinese national character is like. Therefore, if China wants to fundamentally become strong, it must popularize national education and raise the concept of the country. We should set an example for the whole country, sacrificing our families and ourselves, and dedicate our entire bodies to the country, permanently serving as tools of the country and the people. This is the most important point that I, as commander, want to encourage everyone to do together. I hope you will put it into practice."

The Shanghai National Salvation Association of Various Organizations held its 41st executive council meeting at 3:00 PM yesterday. Railway Bureau Proceeds with Restoring the Beijing-Shanghai Transportation 77

The Ministry of Railways Dispatches Personnel to Shanghai to Assist

The Traffic Department Convened a Meeting Yesterday to Discuss Various Measures

The Sino-Japanese armistice and troop withdrawal conference was signed by representatives of both sides yesterday morning as agreed. From now on, military actions will come to an end. The two railway bureaus have already planned to first restore traffic on the Beijing-Shanghai and Songhu (Shanghai-Hangzhou) lines. The details are as follows:

Li Arrives in Shanghai: Yesterday, the Ministry of Railways dispatched Director Li of the General Affairs Department to Shanghai to assist the two railway bureaus in quickly restoring traffic on the Beijing-Shanghai and Songhu lines. He personally came to Shanghai to work with Director Chen of the bureau, Traffic Department Director Zheng Baozhao, and other relevant personnel. Li discussed and planned the implementation measures with Director Chen until around 6:00 PM.

Traffic Meeting: Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, Traffic Department Director Zheng Baozhao also convened key personnel of the Traffic Department to have a detailed discussion on starting to repair the Qingyanggang Railway Bridge and repairing the tracks. The meeting adjourned after 5:00 PM. According to Zheng, the implementation measures for restoring traffic have already been decided. It is expected that the Beijing-Shanghai Railway will be open to traffic in about two weeks. In the future, a temporary station will be set up at the North Station first.

Intensifying Work: The restoration of traffic is being jointly handled by personnel from the Traffic, Engineering, and Mechanical Departments. All bridges and tracks destroyed from Kunshan to the North Station are expected to be completely repaired within about five days. As soon as the Japanese army begins to withdraw, repairs will be rushed. Although yesterday was the anniversary of Sun Yat-sen's inauguration as the Extraordinary President, when work should have been stopped, the bureau still worked all day to carry out all matters related to restoring traffic. The radio station has also been ordered to continue working as usual at night so that it can contact everything at any time.

The Chinese Association for the Protection of Children Welcomes Madam Xiao De 78

Yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM, the Chinese Association for the Protection of Children held a tea party at its Shanghai War Zone Orphanage to welcome Madam Xiao De. A piece of white cloth was hung at the entrance, inscribed with the words "Welcome Madam Xiao De." Inside, the walls were plastered with slogans such as "Welcome the Great Mother," "Promote Parental Education," and "A Wise Mother Must Have a Wise Son," which were very moving. Those who attended included Zhu Qinglan, Mrs. Li Jinlun, Kong Xiangxi (represented by Xu Jianping), Hu Xuanming, Le Lingsheng, Chen Gengya, Zha Liangzhao, Anderson, Fei Wusheng, Mrs. Fu Bulan, Mrs. Wu Weide, Ms. Liu Wang Liming, Ms. Imanli, Ms. Tian Cuibao, Ms. Tang Liyuan, Wang Guanyi, Zhang Yueru, Chen Zhengfan, and more than 200 students from the orphanage. The meeting was chaired by Ms. Liu Wang Liming, vice president of the association, who delivered the opening remarks, stating that "Madam Xiao De is a heroic mother, a great mother, and a wise mother. She cultivated her son to fight for justice and humanity, which is a model for all mothers. With the example of Madam Xiao, the motherly way of the world will shine brightly. We firmly believe that human civilization originates in the cradle, which further increases our courage to promote the cause of protecting children." Then, President Kong Xiangxi gave a speech, stating that "Madam Xiao De's virtue is comparable to Mencius' mother in ancient China. Xiao De's death was not for nationalism but for universalism and for justice and humanity, which further increases our admiration. We deeply hope that Madam Xiao will restrain her grief. Xiao De's death was by no means in vain. The children present today and all over China are prepared to be the second Xiao De, and with the spirit of not fearing death, seek liberation for China itself and peace for the world." When Madam Xiao De stood up to answer, tears welled up in her eyes, which saddened all who saw her. The love of a mother for her son cannot be drowned by water or extinguished by fire. Her voice trembled extremely. Her reply stated, "I have no regrets that my son sacrificed himself for justice and humanity. He belongs to society and humanity, not to his parents privately. Therefore, his sacrifice is extremely right and proper. I came to China this time to bury my son, and I am very grateful for the sincere hospitality I have received from all parties. From what I have seen, China is a country full of potential and hopes to achieve peace and unification at an early date and embark on the path of construction and strength." Then, General Zhu Qinglan stood up and gave a speech, stating that "Xiao De's chivalrous spirit and righteousness are entirely due to his mother's education. For the sake of those of us who come to education and leave a permanent memory, we should urgently raise a large sum of money to establish the Xiao De Education Fund to cultivate geniuses among orphans, from elementary school to middle school to university, to become useful talents for society, to work for China, and to work for the world, so as not to fail Xiao De's sacrifice and Madam Xiao De's mother's education. This kind of commemoration can be called a living commemoration and a permanent commemoration." Everyone present strongly agreed with this suggestion, and then elected Kong Xiangxi, Zhu Qinglan, Fei Wusheng, Mrs. Li Jinlun, and Mrs. Fu Bulan as members of the preparatory committee, responsible for carrying out everything. Finally, Zhang Huaguang, a representative of the elementary school students, gave a speech, expressing his willingness to continue Xiao De's legacy and work hard for China and the world in the future. Madam Xiao De was very moved when she heard this. Afterwards, Chinese and foreign photographers came to take pictures, and Wu Weide and others guided Madam Xiao De to visit the orphanage. The meeting ended at about 6:00 PM.

The Chinese Association for the Protection of Children Welcomes Madam Xiao's Photography 79

Reasons for Consolidating the Postal Foundation and Concrete Plan 80

Proposed by the Shanghai Postal Workers' Union

The Shanghai Postal Workers' Union proposed a concrete plan to consolidate the postal foundation and requested that the Ministry of Communications adopt and implement the outline. The news was published in yesterday's newspaper. The four reasons for the plan are as follows: Reason 1: According to the postal service's opening, it was handled by the customs, and the government did not allocate a single penny. The customs advanced 2,487,000 yuan for the opening expenses. After 1922, the postal service gradually had a surplus and repaid it year by year. By 1926, it was fully repaid. From the same year, the postal service also paid the surplus to the former Ministry of Communications in Beijing. The detailed numbers are as follows:

1922: 855,000 yuan; 1923: 1,850,000 yuan; 1924: 1,940,000 yuan; 1925: 1,890,000 yuan; 1926: 1,990,000 yuan; 1927: 292,000 yuan; a total of 8,817,000 yuan. After the establishment of the National Government's Ministry of Communications, the postal service paid the Ministry of Communications as follows: From 1929, it paid the Ministry of Communications 30,000 yuan per month for regular expenses, 360,000 yuan per year, which was reimbursed in the regular expenditure account of the Postal Administration. 1929: 480,000 yuan (including part of 1928); 1930: 360,000 yuan; 1931: 360,000 yuan; 1932: 120,000 yuan (calculated up to April); a total of 1,320,000 yuan. Since July 1931, the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau has also paid the Ministry of Communications 30,000 yuan per month from the regular expenses, which is also postal money, totaling 300,000 yuan up to April of this year. In addition, the Postal Administration followed the order of the Ministry of Communications and divided the annual surplus equally, half of which was retained by the bureau for construction and development, and half was paid to the ministry, which was said to be used for other construction projects. The detailed numbers are as follows: 1928: 245,000 yuan; 1929: 580,000 yuan; 1930: 484,000 yuan; a total of 1,309,000 yuan. In addition, the Postal Administration was ordered to pay 2,000,000 yuan for the construction of the Ministry's office building in Nanjing Sajiawan. In addition, the Postal Administration was ordered to allocate 1,000,000 yuan for the Ministry of Communications to open the Shanghai-Chengdu airline. In addition, when China National Aviation Corporation was established, the Post Office was ordered to allocate 2,000,000 yuan. In addition, when Eurasia Aviation Corporation was established, the Post Office was again ordered to allocate 500,000 yuan. The total of the above items is 8,429,000 yuan. The actual amount of the current postal deficit is only more than 4,000,000 yuan. The so-called budget shortfall of 10,000,000 yuan includes more than 5,000,000 yuan for construction applications. If it had not been affected by politics for more than ten years, that is, if the principle of "supporting the postal service with the postal service" had been realized, and the postal surplus had only belonged to the postal service, and had not been paid to the Ministry of Communications, and had not borne the cost of opening aviation, then by the end of last year, the postal surplus would have reached 17,724,600 yuan. Even if it had been hit by occasional natural disasters or foreign aggression, and had a deficit of more than 4,000,000 yuan, it would still have had savings of 12,000,000 yuan. Why would it be at a loss and make the people, who have survived so many disasters, bear so much burden? Therefore, the way to maintain the foundation of the postal service lies in maintaining the economic independence of the postal service. In other words, it is the principle of "supporting the postal service with the postal service." The purpose of the state in running the postal service is to facilitate the people, not to make profits. This is the general practice in all countries in the world. Therefore, all countries allocate funds to subsidize the postal service. The postal service in our country is still in its infancy. It is too late to support it. How can we divide its surplus to support other businesses and limit its development, and make its foundation unstable? If it encounters wind and rain, it will feel shaky. This is the first basis of this plan. In addition to the above-mentioned 17,724,600 yuan paid to the Beijing and Nanjing Ministry of Communications and 2,500,000 yuan returned to the customs, the postal service still had a fund of 2,500,000 yuan before the establishment of the Savings and Remittance Bureau, and about 1,000,000 yuan from the self-run insurance. In the annual settlement of the previous year, in the past ten years (since 1922), in addition to expanding business and adding more than 12,350 bureaus and offices and opening up 852,600 miles of postal routes with the progress of culture and commerce, it actually made a surplus of 23,324,600 yuan. Calculated by the average of ten years, there can be 2,300,000 yuan per year. Not only do we not have to worry about the coming of natural disasters, but if we use it to the fullest extent to develop, its rate of progress may be more than what it is today. This is the second basis of this plan. Based on the above two points, and in accordance with the suggestion of Vice Minister Chen of the Ministry of Communications that he should work and handle things on behalf of others, we have proposed the principle of "supporting the postal service with the postal service" so that the money spent by the people for using the postal service (i.e., postage) is effectively used for the postal service and does not flow to other channels. From the perspective of the state's entire plan, transportation businesses are all for the convenience of the people and should not be biased towards the postal service. However, the deficit of the telegraph service is too large, and the aviation administration needs even more money. If we want to use the income of the large-scale postal service to support it, then what is the difference between holding a heavy load of a thousand pounds and ordering a three-foot-tall child to carry it? It will inevitably lead to both sides losing. It is better to first maintain one and help it grow, and then find other ways to remedy the others. If all the surplus, except for 10% for personnel pensions and 20% for the base, is used for the construction and development of the postal service, this fund will accumulate day by day, and even if there are natural disasters in the future, there will be no increase in postal rates. (To be continued)

The Book Industry Re-telegrams to Request the Cancellation of Postage Increase 81

The book industry re-telegraphed the government, saying: (1) To President Lin of the Luoyang National Government, Standing Committee Members Jiang, Wang, and Hu of the Nanjing Central Political Council, the Executive Yuan, the Legislative Yuan, the Control Yuan, the Ministry of Communications, and the Ministry of Education: The increase in postage for books hinders the development of education and culture in the border provinces. The association has repeatedly telegraphed to request the withdrawal of the decision. Recently, it was found that the elementary school textbooks priced at 6 to 12 cents and with an actual price of 80% off, according to the new postal regulations, cost 1 cent for each book for simple postage, with 2 cents for light books and 5 cents for heavy books; 2 cents for simple postage, with 4 cents for light books and 10 cents for heavy books; 3 cents for simple postage, with 6 cents for light books and 15 cents for heavy books. Adding 10 cents for simple registration, the postage for purchasing and sending books and letters back and forth is 12 cents. If all are simply registered, an additional 20 cents is required. After careful calculation, it is shocking. On May 3, it was reported that Vice Minister Chen and Director Qian talked about the new postal regulations and also believed that it did hinder the culture of the border provinces and decided to restore the old regulations. If a gentleman makes a mistake, if he does not know it deeply, but now he knows it and cancels it, it will not only not damage the government's prestige, but also show the government's fairness and selflessness, its compassion for the people's suffering, and its concern for culture. In recent days, out-of-town postal purchases of books have been accompanied by postage based on the old regulations. It is inconvenient for the member bookstores of the association to deliver them according to the old regulations, and they feel at a loss as to what to do, which will only increase the difficulties over time. Therefore, we re-telegraph to request your order, and earnestly request immediate cancellation, and we will be grateful. Shanghai Book Industry Association. (2) To Acting President Qin and all members of the Nanjing Legislative Yuan: On May 1, the Shen Bao reported that the decision of your Yuan and the Ministry of Communications to increase postage was illegal, and requested the government to stop its implementation. This shows that your Yuan upholds the law and is not biased, and does not want to easily increase the burden on the people. We are grateful. On the 3rd, it was reported that Vice Minister Chen Fumu said that the Legislative Yuan had resolved to stop the increase in postage because the matter had not been reviewed and approved by the Yuan. He did not know the details in Shanghai, but he knew that the postage increase would not be stopped because of this. We are deeply surprised. If the Deputy Minister of Communications can ignore the resolution of the Legislative Yuan, then the balance of powers will be lost, and the legislature will be regarded as a sacrificial sheep. No wonder Western newspapers say that this matter can test whether China respects the spirit of legislation and implements the budget and final accounts. We urge you to uphold a just attitude and a fearless spirit, and to stop this kind of postal rate increase that destroys legislation, increases the burden on the people, and hinders culture and education in accordance with the law. We are eagerly waiting. Shanghai Book Industry Association.

Telegram from the Commerce Staff Welfare Committee 83

To the National Government Executive Yuan Legislative Yuan Ministry of Education in Luoyang, the Shanghai Municipal Government, and all sectors of society: During this invasion by the violent Japanese, the General Factory of the Commercial Press in Zhabei was destroyed, and the families of all employees suffered the same devastating calamity. The employees are displaced and suffering immensely. It has been three months, and the company authorities have repeatedly failed to provide any relief or support to the employees since the incident, harboring ulterior motives with the stored funds and refusing withdrawals in an attempt to cut off their economic lifeline. Recently, the company has established a new factory in Shanghai, and the printing plants in Beiping and Hong Kong have been greatly expanded. Dozens of branches have also never ceased operation. We had hoped to resume work immediately and alleviate the suffering, but the company has suddenly become even more ruthless, falsely reporting to the authorities in an attempt to dismiss all employees, taking advantage of the national crisis to expand personal power. The Municipal Social Bureau not only fails to severely reprimand this behavior but even tends to approve it, allowing the capitalists to deprive the workers of their various legitimate interests. Upon hearing this news, the committee is extremely alarmed. We have observed that since the Shanghai Incident, the Municipal Social Bureau has repeatedly announced that factories are not allowed to take advantage of the situation to attempt dismissals. Now, for the cultural laborers who have suffered significant devastation from the Japanese invaders for many years, we have not heard of any relief from the Bureau. If the Bureau listens to the capitalists and dismisses all employees amidst the extremely challenging recovery situation, watching thousands of employees leave the factory they have worked hard to build for thirty-six years to become unemployed vagrants, it would not only violate the Bureau's own laws but also disregard the workers' hardship. How could a government under the clear blue sky do such a thing? The committee is in a state of extreme anxiety at this critical moment. We can only beg for compassion for the employees who have contributed to the nation's culture and provide relief to them in this desperate situation. We implore you to order the Bureau not to rely on the capitalists' one-sided story and to disregard the truth of the facts, sacrificing the jobs and legal rights of four thousand employees, and to order the company to find ways to resume work and not to attempt dismissals arbitrarily. We also seek the public opinion of all sectors of society. We would be immensely grateful, not only for the sake of the employees but also for the sake of society. We respectfully send this telegram for your consideration. From the Shanghai Commercial Press Employee Relief Committee.

Taxpayers' Association Protests Minimum Electricity Fee Again 87

Practical and Actual Collection is Still the Most Reasonable

Two-Thirds of the Meter Deposit Should be Returned

The Taxpayers' Association sent another letter to the Public Works Department yesterday regarding the minimum electricity fee and meter deposit of the electricity company, saying: "To the Shanghai Public Concession Public Works Department, regarding the case of the Shanghai Electric Power Company's minimum electricity fee and the return of two-thirds of the meter deposit, your bureau replied that the monthly minimum electricity fee is one tael and two and a half qian of silver. As for the meter deposit, the bureau is already in the process of returning part of it, etc. The association believes that the amount of the returned meter deposit should be determined as two-thirds of the amount collected when it was collected every three months. There is no legal reason to change it. The Shanghai Electric Power Company's statement published in the newspaper yesterday seems unwilling to return two-thirds. The reasons it stated are not sufficient to explain the situation when it was collected every three months. When collecting electricity fees every three months, it may not be necessary to collect them outside of three months, so the meter deposit set at that time has been considered. Now it has been changed to collecting once a month, so the guarantee required should only be one-third of the previous one. Moreover, the delay in collection is a matter for the company, what does it have to do with the users? Users have no obligation to bear more stagnant funds. The statement also made many statements about the minimum electricity fee, but according to the observation of the association, practical and actual collection is still legal and reasonable. The company's investment is originally a whole, and the income from electricity fees, if it only belongs to production costs, the association's observation is of course wrong, otherwise, this method is extremely contrary to the law. Since it is not a contract system, it should be practical and actual collection. As for the bill, it will be delivered immediately after it is sent. Correspondently, please investigate and handle it according to the association's opinion and instruct the Shanghai Electric Power Company to handle it. This is to the Shanghai Public Concession Public Works Department."

Their arrogance was overwhelming. Under this special circumstance, it cannot be measured by normal circumstances. Even if it cannot be implemented for a while, this donation cannot be reduced or exempted immediately, but it seems reasonable to give a little time due to the environment. Why did you suddenly use this threatening method? The so-called deadline for payment and the lawsuit after the deadline were not seen at all from the Westerner, and all of them were made by the translator himself, which is even more shocking. In addition to writing to the Finance Committee to request a reduction, I will report the situation to the meeting truthfully. After investigating that the Japanese soldiers' invasion of Shanghai this time has resulted in the complete loss of normality and the exhaustion of the social economy, all unstable forces, and all those who have interests, are trying to eliminate them in order to restore normality as soon as possible. The taxpayers and your bureau should strive for effective cooperation and work together to overcome this difficulty. Unexpectedly, the translator Wang did not know the meaning of the taxpayers and your bureau, abused his power, and threatened them, which is enough to cause misunderstandings and cause disputes. Your bureau should especially maintain the education career of the college to show respect for the taxpayers and the importance of education. According to the previous letter, I respectfully request you to investigate, in addition to exempting the college from the total donation, and to punish the translator Wang for abusing his power and provoking resentment. This is to the Chief of the Shanghai Public Concession Public Works Department."
